<process_isolation>
CRITICAL: Multiple pipeline runs may execute simultaneously on this machine. `ps aux | grep method.py` matches ALL runs, not just yours.
- NEVER kill processes by name (`killall`, `pkill -f`, `ps aux | grep ... | xargs kill`). This kills OTHER runs' processes.
- NEVER monitor processes by name (`ps aux | grep method.py`). You will see other runs' processes and get confused.
- ALWAYS use PID-based process management:
  Run: `uv run method.py & PID=$!` or `timeout <seconds> uv run method.py & PID=$!`
  Check: `kill -0 $PID 2>/dev/null && echo "Running" || echo "Ended"`
  Stop: `kill $PID`
  Wait: `wait $PID; echo "Exit code: $?"`
  Monitor: `tail -f logs/run.log & TAIL_PID=$!` then `kill $TAIL_PID` when done
</process_isolation>

### [3] SYSTEM-USER prompt · 2026-07-18 16:34:32 UTC

````
<hypothesis>
kind: hypothesis
title: Evaluate thermodynamic entropy calibration for LLMs
hypothesis: >-
  Physics-inspired calibration methods that adjust per-sample temperature based on predictive entropy and decision margin
  can provide interpretable confidence calibration for LLM classifiers, though their empirical advantage over standard temperature
  scaling remains unproven and may be limited to specific scenarios such as heterogeneous miscalibration patterns or multi-class
  settings with class-conditional effects. The primary potential novelty lies in inference-time temperature annealing (currently
  unimplemented) rather than post-hoc calibration.
motivation: >-
  LLM classifiers often exhibit overconfidence, which undermines reliability in high-stakes applications. A physics-inspired
  calibration method that treats uncertainty as entropy could provide a principled, model-agnostic way to improve trustworthiness
  without extensive retraining.
assumptions:
- >-
  Predictive uncertainty in LLMs can be meaningfully analogized to thermodynamic entropy.
- >-
  Temperature-based annealing during inference does not severely degrade classification accuracy.
- >-
  The entropy of the output distribution correlates with true error probability in a way that can be adjusted via temperature
  scaling.
investigation_approach: >-
  Implement a temperature-annealing schedule during decoding or final-layer logit adjustment, compute entropy-based uncertainty
  metrics, and evaluate calibration error (ECE, Brier score) on standard classification benchmarks compared to baseline temperature
  scaling and other calibration methods.
success_criteria: >-
  The proposed method achieves statistically significant lower expected calibration error (ECE) and Brier score compared to
  standard temperature scaling and uncalibrated baselines, while maintaining or improving accuracy on held-out test sets.
related_works:
- >-
  Temperature scaling (Guo et al., 2017) calibrates by tuning a single temperature parameter on validation data; our approach
  differs by using an annealing schedule inspired by thermodynamic principles rather than a fixed scaling factor.
- >-
  Entropy-based uncertainty estimation (e.g., in Bayesian neural networks) uses Shannon entropy of predictive distributions;
  we extend this by explicitly linking entropy to a thermodynamic analogy and incorporating an annealing procedure during
  inference.
inspiration: >-
  Thermodynamic entropy and temperature annealing from statistical physics, where entropy measures disorder and temperature
  controls the system's exploration of states; adapted to the context of LLM predictive distributions.
terms:
- term: Expected Calibration Error (ECE)
  definition: >-
    A metric that measures the difference between a model's predicted confidence and its actual accuracy by binning predictions
    and computing weighted absolute differences.
- term: Temperature scaling
  definition: >-
    A post-hoc calibration method that divides logits by a scalar temperature parameter before applying softmax to adjust
    confidence scores.
- term: Thermodynamic entropy
  definition: >-
    A physical quantity representing the amount of disorder or randomness in a system, often used in statistical mechanics
    to describe the distribution of microstates.
- term: Annealing
  definition: >-
    A process of gradually changing a control parameter (like temperature) to allow a system to reach a more stable or optimal
    state, commonly used in optimization and physics.
summary: >-
  This hypothesis proposes a physics-inspired calibration method that treats LLM predictive uncertainty as thermodynamic entropy
  and uses temperature annealing during inference to improve confidence calibration.
_relation_rationale: >-
  Refined to acknowledge negative results; narrowed from universal claim to conditional/scenario-specific
_confidence_delta: decreased
_key_changes:
- >-
  Removed claim that method 'produces better-calibrated confidence scores' - evidence shows TS outperforms TEC
- >-
  Added caveat that empirical advantage 'remains unproven' given experimental results
- >-
  Narrowed scope to 'specific scenarios' (heterogeneous miscalibration, multi-class) not yet tested
- Clarified that inference-time annealing is unimplemented potential novelty
- Shifted from positive performance claim to evaluative/exploratory framing
relation_type: evolution
</hypothesis>

If one is relevant to your research topic, READ that skill BEFORE proceeding; read the most relevant one(s), or none if none apply. approach: >-

  DBpedia (or appropriate pre-trained models for each dataset). Generate real logits (not synthetic). Implement: (1) Uncalibrated
  baseline, (2) Temperature Scaling (tune T on validation for ECE), (3) TEC with expanded hyperparameter search (T_0 in [0.1,
  20.0], alpha in [0, 2], beta in [0, 1], tune for ECE). Create heterogeneous splits: easy (high margin) vs hard (low margin)
  examples. Metrics: ECE (primary), Brier, NLL, accuracy. Bootstrap CI (1000 samples). Test: Does TEC outperform TS on multi-class
  or heterogeneous scenarios?
depends_on:

  label: datasets

  relation_rationale:
</artifact_direction>

summary: >-
  Successfully collected 5 diverse text classification datasets from HuggingFace Hub for LLM calibration evaluation. Datasets
  include binary (SST-2, QNLI) and multi-class (AG News with 4 classes, MNLI with 3 classes, DBpedia with 14 classes) classification
  tasks with varying difficulty levels. All datasets were standardized to a unified JSON schema with text input, integer labels
  (0-indexed), and metadata fields. Train/validation/test splits were created with stratified sampling to preserve class distribution.
  Validation sets are sized appropriately for temperature tuning (1-5K examples). The datasets were transformed to exp_sel_data_out.json
  schema format with 150,000 total examples across 5 datasets. Full, mini (15 examples), and preview (15 examples, truncated)
  variants were generated. All files passed JSON schema validation. Total dataset size is 116MB (under 300MB limit). The datasets

```
Let me analyze this task carefully. I need to create a detailed plan for an experiment that evaluates thermodynamic entropy calibration (TEC) for LLMs compared to temperature scaling (TS) and baselines.

Let me break down what I have:
1. Hypothesis: Physics-inspired calibration methods (TEC) may provide interpretable confidence calibration for LLM classifiers, though empirical advantage over TS remains unproven
2. Artifact direction: Evaluate TEC, TS, and baselines on real LLM embeddings across 5 datasets, testing heterogeneous miscalibration scenarios
3. Dependencies: Dataset artifact with 5 text classification datasets (SST-2, QNLI, AG News, MNLI, DBpedia)

The plan needs to be:
- Specific and actionable
- Include implementation pseudocode
- Have a fallback plan
- Have a testing plan
- Use the gpu compute profile (since we're working with transformer models)

Let me think about what the experiment should do:
1. Load pre-trained transformers (DistilBERT, RoBERTa, BERT) via HuggingFace
2. Generate real logits for the 5 datasets
3. Implement 3 methods:
   - Uncalibrated baseline
   - Temperature Scaling (tune T on validation)
   - TEC with hyperparameter search
4. Create heterogeneous splits (easy vs hard examples)
5. Compute metrics: ECE, Brier, NLL, accuracy
6. Bootstrap CI
7. Compare TEC vs TS on multi-class and heterogeneous scenarios

For the compute profile, since we're using transformer models and need to generate embeddings/logits, we should use the 'gpu' profile.

Let me structure this as a proper plan:

Title: Should be short, plain language, 4-8 words
Summary: Brief overview
Implementation pseudocode: High-level steps
Fallback plan: What to do if primary approach fails


Testing plan: How to validate

I'll develop a comprehensive strategy for testing the calibration methods. The key is to create a robust validation approach that can definitively compare TEC and TS across different scenarios. I'll design a multi-stage testing protocol that systematically evaluates the calibration performance, focusing on identifying nuanced differences in uncertainty estimation
```

### [21] TOOL RESULT — invoke_skill · 2026-07-18 16:35:21 UTC

````
{"content": [{"cache_prompt": false, "type": "text", "text": "## Web tools\n\nYou have three web capabilities: **search**, **fetch**, and **grep** (exact\nregex extraction over a full page or PDF).\n\n**Pick where they come from, in this order:**\n\n1. **If you have built-in `WebSearch` / `WebFetch` tools, PREFER those over the\n   scripts below.** They may be **deferred tools** (listed by name but with\n   schemas not yet loaded) \u2014 if so, call `ToolSearch(\"select:WebSearch,WebFetch\")`\n   ONCE to load them, then use them normally. Do not skip them just because they\n   need that one extra load step; they are the preferred path. Pair them with the\n   `aii_web_tools__fetch_grep` script below when you need exact text / numbers /\n   methodology that a summary would miss, or when reading a PDF.\n2. **Only if you have NO built-in `WebSearch` / `WebFetch`** (e.g. the OpenHands\n   backend), use the scripts in this skill (below). They are our own\n   implementations \u2014 Serper.dev for search, html2text + PyMuPDF for fetch, and\n   regex grep over the full document text. {
  "command": "create",
  "path": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_3fUR0i5e8NC7/3_invention_loop/iter_2/gen_plan/gen_plan_experiment_1/.sdk_openhands_agent_struct_out.json",
  "file_text": "{\n  \"title\": \"Evaluate TEC vs TS Calibration on LLM Embeddings\",\n  \"summary\": \"Test thermodynamic entropy calibration against temperature scaling on 5 text classification datasets using pre-trained transformers, with heterogeneous split analysis and bootstrap confidence intervals.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"gpu\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Experimental Setup\\n\\n### Dataset Preparation\\n1. Load the standardized datasets from the dependency artifact (full_data_out.json)\\n2. For each dataset, load the appropriate pre-trained model:\\n   - SST-2: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english\\n   - QNLI: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english (or BERT-base)\\n   - AG News: roberta-base (fine-tuned on AG News)\\n   - MNLI: roberta-large-mnli (or roberta-base)\\n   - DBpedia: bert-base-uncased (fine-tuned on DBpedia)\\n3. Split each dataset into:\\n   - Train (60%): for model fine-tuning if needed\\n   - Validation (20%): for hyperparameter tuning\\n   - Test (20%): for final evaluation\\n\\n### Model & Logit Extraction\\n```python\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import AutoModelForSequenceClassification, AutoTokenizer\\nfrom torch.utils.data import DataLoader\\nimport json\\n\\n# Load dataset\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Model mapping\\ndataset_models = {\\n    'sst-2': 'distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english',\\n    'qnli': 'bert-base-uncased',  # May need QNLI fine-tuned version\\n    'ag_news': 'roberta-base',  # May need AG News fine-tuned\\n    'mnli': 'roberta-large-mnli',\\n    'dbpedia': 'bert-base-uncased'  # May need DBpedia fine-tuned\\n}\\n\\n# Extract logits for each dataset\\nfor dataset_name, model_name in dataset_models.items():\\n    tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model = AutoModelForSequenceClassification.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model.eval()\\n    \\n    # Get dataset examples\\n    dataset = [d for d in data['datasets'] if d['dataset'] == dataset_name][0]\\n    examples = dataset['examples']\\n    \\n    # Extract logits (no gradient)\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        for ex in examples:\\n            inputs = tokenizer(ex['input'], return_tensors='pt', truncation=True, padding=True)\\n            outputs = model(**inputs)\\n            logits = outputs.logits\\n            # Store logits with example\\n            ex['logits'] = logits.numpy().tolist()\\n            ex['num_classes'] = logits.shape[-1]\\n```\\n\\n### Method 1: Uncalibrated Baseline\\n```python\\ndef uncalibrated_predictions(logits):\\n    # Softmax without temperature scaling\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1)\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values\\n    return preds, confs, probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 2: Temperature Scaling (TS)\\n```python\\nimport torch.nn as nn\\nimport torch.optim as optim\\n\\ndef temperature_scaling(logits, labels, val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Tune temperature T on validation set to minimize NLL.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Initialize temperature\\n    temperature = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1) * 1.0)\\n    optimizer = optim.LBFGS([temperature], lr=0.01, max_iter=50)\\n    \\n    logits_tensor = torch.tensor(logits)\\n    labels_tensor = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    \\n    def eval():\\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\\n        scaled_logits = logits_tensor / temperature\\n        loss = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()(scaled_logits, labels_tensor)\\n        loss.backward()\\n        return loss\\n    \\n    # Optimize temperature\\n    for _ in range(100):\\n        optimizer.step(eval)\\n    \\n    # Apply to validation set\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        val_scaled = torch.tensor(val_logits) / temperature\\n        val_probs = torch.softmax(val_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        val_preds = torch.argmax(val_probs, dim=-1)\\n        val_confs = torch.max(val_probs, dim=-1).values\\n    \\n    return temperature.item(), val_preds, val_confs, val_probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 3: Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration (TEC)\\n```python\\ndef compute_entropy(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Shannon entropy of probability distribution.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    epsilon = 1e-12\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, epsilon, 1.0 - epsilon)\\n    entropy = -torch.sum(probs * torch.log(probs), dim=-1)\\n    return entropy\\n\\ndef compute_margin(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute decision margin (difference between top-2 predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sorted_probs, _ = torch.sort(probs, dim=-1, descending=True)\\n    margin = sorted_probs[..., 0] - sorted_probs[..., 1]\\n    return margin\\n\\ndef tec_calibration(logits, T_0, alpha, beta):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration.\\n    \\n    Adjusts per-sample temperature based on entropy and margin:\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy - beta * margin)\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits (N, C)\\n        T_0: Base temperature parameter\\n        alpha: Entropy weight parameter\\n        beta: Margin weight parameter\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Calibrated probabilities\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    entropy = compute_entropy(probs)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Normalize entropy and margin to [0, 1]\\n    max_entropy = torch.log(torch.tensor(probs.shape[-1]).float())\\n    norm_entropy = entropy / max_entropy\\n    norm_margin = margin  # Already in [0, 1]\\n    \\n    # Compute per-sample temperature\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * norm_entropy - beta * norm_margin)\\n    T_sample = torch.clamp(T_sample, min=0.01, max=100.0)  # Prevent extremes\\n    \\n    # Apply temperature scaling per sample\\n    # Need to handle per-sample temperature\\n    scaled_logits = torch.tensor(logits) / T_sample.unsqueeze(-1)\\n    calibrated_probs = torch.softmax(scaled_logits, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    return calibrated_probs, T_sample\\n\\ndef tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Grid search for TEC hyperparameters.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    best_ece = float('inf')\\n    best_params = None\\n    \\n    T_0_range = [0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, 10.0, 20.0]\\n    alpha_range = [0.0, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0]\\n    beta_range = [0.0, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1.0]\\n    \\n    for T_0 in T_0_range:\\n        for alpha in alpha_range:\\n            for beta in beta_range:\\n                probs, _ = tec_calibration(val_logits, T_0, alpha, beta)\\n                ece = compute_ece(probs, val_labels)\\n                \\n                if ece < best_ece:\\n                    best_ece = ece\\n                    best_params = (T_0, alpha, beta)\\n    \\n    return best_params, best_ece\\n```\\n\\n### Heterogeneous Split Creation\\n```python\\ndef create_heterogeneous_splits(logits, labels, easy_ratio=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Split dataset into easy (high margin) and hard (low margin) examples.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits\\n        labels: True labels\\n        easy_ratio: Ratio of easy examples to include\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        easy_indices, hard_indices\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Sort by margin\\n    sorted_indices = torch.argsort(margin, descending=True)\\n    \\n    n_easy = int(len(sorted_indices) * easy_ratio)\\n    easy_indices = sorted_indices[:n_easy]\\n    hard_indices = sorted_indices[n_easy:]\\n    \\n    return easy_indices, hard_indices\\n```\\n\\n### Metrics Computation\\n```python\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import brier_score_loss\\n\\ndef compute_ece(probs, labels, n_bins=10):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Expected Calibration Error.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_bins: Number of bins for calibration\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        ECE value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Get confidence and predictions\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values.numpy()\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1).numpy()\\n    labels = np.array(labels)\\n    \\n    # Bin predictions\\n    bins = np.linspace(0, 1, n_bins + 1)\\n    ece = 0.0\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bins):\\n        mask = (confs >= bins[i]) & (confs < bins[i + 1])\\n        if mask.sum() > 0:\\n            bin_acc = np.mean(preds[mask] == labels[mask])\\n            bin_conf = np.mean(confs[mask])\\n            ece += np.abs(bin_acc - bin_conf) * mask.sum() / len(confs)\\n    \\n    return ece\\n\\ndef compute_nll(probs, labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Negative Log-Likelihood.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, min=1e-12, max=1.0)\\n    labels = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    nll = -torch.log(probs[torch.arange(len(labels)), labels]).mean()\\n    return nll.item()\\n\\ndef compute_brier_score(probs, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Brier Score.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # One-hot encode labels\\n    labels_onehot = torch.zeros(len(labels), n_classes)\\n    labels_onehot.scatter_(1, torch.tensor(labels).unsqueeze(1), 1)\\n    \\n    brier = torch.mean((probs - labels_onehot) ** 2).item()\\n    return brier\\n\\ndef bootstrap_ci(metric_func, probs, labels, n_bootstrap=1000, confidence=0.95):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute bootstrap confidence interval for a metric.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        metric_func: Function that computes metric\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities\\n        labels: True labels\\n        n_bootstrap: Number of bootstrap samples\\n        confidence: Confidence level\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (mean, lower_ci, upper_ci)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs_np = probs.numpy()\\n    labels_np = np.array(labels)\\n    n = len(labels_np)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = []\\n    for _ in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        boot_probs = probs_np[indices]\\n        boot_labels = labels_np[indices]\\n        metric = metric_func(torch.tensor(boot_probs), boot_labels)\\n        bootstrap_metrics.append(metric)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = np.array(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    mean = np.mean(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    lower = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 - confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    upper = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 + confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    \\n    return mean, lower, upper\\n```\\n\\n### Main Experiment Loop\\n```python\\ndef run_experiment(dataset_name, logits, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Run full experiment for one dataset.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        dataset_name: Name of dataset\\n        logits: Extracted logits (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_classes: Number of classes\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Dictionary of results\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Split data\\n    n = len(labels)\\n    indices = np.random.permutation(n)\\n    train_idx = indices[:int(0.6 * n)]\\n    val_idx = indices[int(0.6 * n):int(0.8 * n)]\\n    test_idx = indices[int(0.8 * n):]\\n    \\n    # Prepare splits\\n    train_logits = [logits[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    train_labels = [labels[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    val_logits = [logits[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    val_labels = [labels[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    test_logits = [logits[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    test_labels = [labels[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    \\n    results = {'dataset': dataset_name}\\n    \\n    # Method 1: Uncalibrated\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Uncalibrated ===\\\")\\n    test_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(test_logits), dim=-1)\\n    test_preds = torch.argmax(test_probs, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece = compute_ece(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    brier = compute_brier_score(test_probs, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll = compute_nll(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    acc = (test_preds == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['uncalibrated'] = {\\n        'ece': ece,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci,\\n        'brier': brier,\\n        'nll': nll,\\n        'accuracy': acc\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 2: Temperature Scaling\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Temperature Scaling ===\\\")\\n    T_opt, val_preds, val_confs, val_probs = temperature_scaling(\\n        val_logits, val_labels, val_logits, val_labels\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal T to test set\\n    test_scaled = torch.tensor(test_logits) / T_opt\\n    test_probs_ts = torch.softmax(test_scaled, dim=-1)\\n    test_preds_ts = torch.argmax(test_probs_ts, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_ts = compute_ece(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    brier_ts = compute_brier_score(test_probs_ts, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_ts = compute_nll(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    acc_ts = (test_preds_ts == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_ts = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['temperature_scaling'] = {\\n        'T_optimal': T_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_ts,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_ts,\\n        'brier': brier_ts,\\n        'nll': nll_ts,\\n        'accuracy': acc_ts\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 3: TEC\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: TEC ===\\\")\\n    best_params, best_ece_val = tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels)\\n    T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt = best_params\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal TEC to test set\\n    test_probs_tec, test_T_sample = tec_calibration(\\n        test_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n    )\\n    test_preds_tec = torch.argmax(test_probs_tec, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_tec = compute_ece(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    brier_tec = compute_brier_score(test_probs_tec, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_tec = compute_nll(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    acc_tec = (test_preds_tec == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_tec = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['tec'] = {\\n        'T_0_optimal': T_0_opt,\\n        'alpha_optimal': alpha_opt,\\n        'beta_optimal': beta_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_tec,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_tec,\\n        'brier': brier_tec,\\n        'nll': nll_tec,\\n        'accuracy': acc_tec\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Heterogeneous Split Analysis\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Heterogeneous Split Analysis ===\\\")\\n    easy_idx, hard_idx = create_heterogeneous_splits(test_logits, test_labels)\\n    \\n    for split_name, split_idx in [('easy', easy_idx), ('hard', hard_idx)]:\\n        split_logits = [test_logits[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        split_labels = [test_labels[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        \\n        # Uncalibrated\\n        split_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(split_logits), dim=-1)\\n        ece_split = compute_ece(split_probs, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TS\\n        split_scaled = torch.tensor(split_logits) / T_opt\\n        split_probs_ts = torch.softmax(split_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        ece_ts_split = compute_ece(split_probs_ts, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TEC\\n        split_probs_tec, _ = tec_calibration(\\n            split_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n        )\\n        ece_tec_split = compute_ece(split_probs_tec, split_labels)\\n        \\n        results[f'heterogeneous_{split_name}'] = {\\n            'n_samples': len(split_idx),\\n            'uncalibrated_ece': ece_split,\\n            'ts_ece': ece_ts_split,\\n            'tec_ece': ece_tec_split\\n        }\\n    \\n    return results\\n```\\n\\n### Output Format\\n```python\\ndef save_results(all_results, filename='method_out.json'):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Save results to method_out.json.\\n    \\n    Format:\\n    {\\n        \\\"experiment\\\": \\\"TEC_vs_TS_evaluation\\\",\\n        \\\"datasets\\\": [\\n            {\\n                \\\"dataset\\\": \\\"sst-2\\\",\\n                \\\"n_classes\\\": 2,\\n                \\\"results\\\": {\\n                    \\\"uncalibrated\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"temperature_scaling\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"tec\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_easy\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_hard\\\": {...}\\n                }\\n            },\\n            ...\\n        ],\\n        \\\"summary\\\": {\\n            \\\"teec_better_than_ts_count\\\": 2,\\n            \\\"ts_better_than_teec_count\\\": 3,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_ts\\\": 0.05,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_tec\\\": 0.03\\n        }\\n    }\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    with open(filename, 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(all_results, f, indent=2)\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## Fallback Plan\\n\\n### Issue 1: Pre-trained Models Not Available/Fail to Load\\n**Symptoms:** Unable to load HuggingFace models, model download fails, out of memory.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Use smaller/distilled versions of models:\\n   - Use `distilbert-base-uncased` instead of BERT/RoBERTa\\n   - Use `bert-base-uncased` with minimal fine-tuning on each dataset\\n2. If still failing, use synthetic logits sampled from real distribution:\\n   - Fit a simple classifier (LogisticRegression) on each dataset\\n   - Extract decision function values as \\\"logits\\\"\\n   - Use these as approximation of LLM logits\\n\\n### Issue 2: TEC Hyperparameter Tuning Too Slow\\n**Symptoms:** Grid search takes too long, exceeds time budget.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Reduce hyperparameter grid:\\n   - T_0: [0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0]\\n   - alpha: [0.0, 1.0, 2.0]\\n   - beta: [0.0, 0.5, 1.0]\\n2. Use random search instead of grid search (sample 20 combinations)\\n3. Use validation ECE as objective (faster than cross-validation)\\n\\n### Issue 3: GPU Memory Insufficient for Large Models\\n**Symptoms:** OOM errors when loading models or processing data.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Process data in smaller batches (batch_size=8 or 16)\\n2. Use CPU for inference (slower but works):\\n   ```python\\n   model.cpu()\\n   torch.set_num_threads(4)  # Use multiple CPU threads\\n   ```\\n3. Use gradient checkpointing or model quantization (8-bit)\\n\\n### Issue 4: Bootstrap CI Computation Too Slow\\n**Symptoms:** 1000 bootstrap samples take too long.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Reduce to 100 bootstrap samples\\n2. Use analytical CI approximation if distribution is approximately normal\\n3. Compute only ECE and skip CI if time is critical\\n\\n### Issue 5: TEC Implementation Unclear or Fails\\n**Symptoms:** TEC formula unclear from hypothesis, implementation produces NaNs or poor results.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Simplify TEC to basic form:\\n   - Use only entropy-based adjustment: `T = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy)`\\n   - Or only margin-based: `T = T_0 * (1 - beta * margin)`\\n2. Compare multiple TEC variants:\\n   - TEC-entropy (entropy only)\\n   - TEC-margin (margin only)\\n   - TEC-full (both)\\n3. If all fail, treat as ablation study: \\\"TEC variants fail to outperform TS\\\"\\n\\n### Issue 6: Datasets Too Large to Process\\n**Symptoms:** Processing all 150K examples exceeds time budget.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Use subset of data:\\n   - Sample 10K examples per dataset (stratified by class)\\n   - Ensure validation set has at least 1K examples for tuning\\n2. Process only 3 datasets instead of 5:\\n   - Prioritize: SST-2 (binary), MNLI (3-class), DBpedia (14-class)\\n   - Covers binary, few-class, many-class scenarios\\n\\n### Issue 7: Metrics Computation Errors\\n**Symptoms:** ECE computation produces unreasonable values, Brier score formula incorrect.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. Use standard library implementations:\\n   - Use `sklearn.calibration.calibration_curve` for ECE\\n   - Verify Brier score with `sklearn.metrics.brier_score_loss` (for binary)\\n   - For multi-class, implement as MSE between probs and one-hot labels\\n2. Test metrics on simple cases first:\\n   - Perfect calibration: probs = accuracies in each bin\\n   - Random predictions: ECE should be high\\n3. Visualize reliability diagrams to verify ECE computation\\n\\n### Minimum Viable Experiment (if all else fails)\\nIf multiple issues compound and time is running out:\\n1. Run only on SST-2 dataset (smallest, simplest)\\n2. Compare only Uncalibrated vs Temperature Scaling (skip TEC)\\n3. Compute only ECE and accuracy (skip Brier, NLL, bootstrap CI)\\n4. Use 1K examples for fast iteration\\n5. Document as \\\"pilot study\\\" and note limitations\",\n  \"testing_plan\": \"## Testing Plan\\n\\n### Phase 1: Quick Sanity Check (15 minutes)\\n**Goal:** Verify data loading and model access work.\\n\\n```python\\n# Test 1: Load dependency dataset\\nimport json\\nwith open('../iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1/full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\nprint(f\\\"Loaded data['datasets'][0]['examples'][:10]\\nwith torch.no_grad():\\n    for ex in sample_examples:\\n        inputs = tokenizer(ex['input'], return_tensors='pt', truncation=True)\\n        outputs = Load the standardized datasets from the dependency artifact (full_data_out.json)\\n2. For each dataset, load the appropriate pre-trained model:\\n   - SST-2: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english\\n   - QNLI: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english (or BERT-base)\\n   - AG News: roberta-base (fine-tuned on AG News)\\n   - MNLI: roberta-large-mnli (or roberta-base)\\n   - DBpedia: bert-base-uncased (fine-tuned on DBpedia)\\n3. Split each dataset into:\\n   - Train (60%): for model fine-tuning if needed\\n   - Validation (20%): for hyperparameter tuning\\n   - Test (20%): for final evaluation\\n\\n### Model & Logit Extraction\\n```python\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import AutoModelForSequenceClassification, AutoTokenizer\\nfrom torch.utils.data import DataLoader\\nimport json\\n\\n# Load dataset\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Model mapping\\ndataset_models = {\\n    'sst-2': 'distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english',\\n    'qnli': 'bert-base-uncased',  # May need QNLI fine-tuned version\\n    'ag_news': 'roberta-base',  # May need AG News fine-tuned\\n    'mnli': 'roberta-large-mnli',\\n    'dbpedia': 'bert-base-uncased'  # May need DBpedia fine-tuned\\n}\\n\\n# Extract logits for each dataset\\nfor dataset_name, model_name in dataset_models.items():\\n    tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model = AutoModelForSequenceClassification.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model.eval()\\n    \\n    # Get dataset examples\\n    dataset = [d for d in data['datasets'] if d['dataset'] == dataset_name][0]\\n    examples = dataset['examples']\\n    \\n    # Extract logits (no gradient)\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        for ex in examples:\\n            inputs = tokenizer(ex['input'], return_tensors='pt', truncation=True, padding=True)\\n            outputs = model(**inputs)\\n            logits = outputs.logits\\n            # Store logits with example\\n            ex['logits'] = logits.numpy().tolist()\\n            ex['num_classes'] = logits.shape[-1]\\n```\\n\\n### Method 1: Uncalibrated Baseline\\n```python\\ndef uncalibrated_predictions(logits):\\n    # Softmax without temperature scaling\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1)\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values\\n    return preds, confs, probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 2: Temperature Scaling (TS)\\n```python\\nimport torch.nn as nn\\nimport torch.optim as optim\\n\\ndef temperature_scaling(logits, labels, val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Tune temperature T on validation set to minimize NLL.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Initialize temperature\\n    temperature = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1) * 1.0)\\n    optimizer = optim.LBFGS([temperature], lr=0.01, max_iter=50)\\n    \\n    logits_tensor = torch.tensor(logits)\\n    labels_tensor = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    \\n    def eval():\\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\\n        scaled_logits = logits_tensor / temperature\\n        loss = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()(scaled_logits, labels_tensor)\\n        loss.backward()\\n        return loss\\n    \\n    # Optimize temperature\\n    for _ in range(100):\\n        optimizer.step(eval)\\n    \\n    # Apply to validation set\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        val_scaled = torch.tensor(val_logits) / temperature\\n        val_probs = torch.softmax(val_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        val_preds = torch.argmax(val_probs, dim=-1)\\n        val_confs = torch.max(val_probs, dim=-1).values\\n    \\n    return temperature.item(), val_preds, val_confs, val_probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 3: Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration (TEC)\\n```python\\ndef compute_entropy(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Shannon entropy of probability distribution.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    epsilon = 1e-12\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, epsilon, 1.0 - epsilon)\\n    entropy = -torch.sum(probs * torch.log(probs), dim=-1)\\n    return entropy\\n\\ndef compute_margin(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute decision margin (difference between top-2 predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sorted_probs, _ = torch.sort(probs, dim=-1, descending=True)\\n    margin = sorted_probs[..., 0] - sorted_probs[..., 1]\\n    return margin\\n\\ndef tec_calibration(logits, T_0, alpha, beta):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration.\\n    \\n    Adjusts per-sample temperature based on entropy and margin:\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy - beta * margin)\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits (N, C)\\n        T_0: Base temperature parameter\\n        alpha: Entropy weight parameter\\n        beta: Margin weight parameter\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Calibrated probabilities\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    entropy = compute_entropy(probs)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Normalize entropy and margin to [0, 1]\\n    max_entropy = torch.log(torch.tensor(probs.shape[-1]).float())\\n    norm_entropy = entropy / max_entropy\\n    norm_margin = margin  # Already in [0, 1]\\n    \\n    # Compute per-sample temperature\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * norm_entropy - beta * norm_margin)\\n    T_sample = torch.clamp(T_sample, min=0.01, max=100.0)  # Prevent extremes\\n    \\n    # Apply temperature scaling per sample\\n    # Need to handle per-sample temperature\\n    scaled_logits = torch.tensor(logits) / T_sample.unsqueeze(-1)\\n    calibrated_probs = torch.softmax(scaled_logits, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    return calibrated_probs, T_sample\\n\\ndef tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Grid search for TEC hyperparameters.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    best_ece = float('inf')\\n    best_params = None\\n    \\n    T_0_range = [0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, 10.0, 20.0]\\n    alpha_range = [0.0, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0]\\n    beta_range = [0.0, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1.0]\\n    \\n    for T_0 in T_0_range:\\n        for alpha in alpha_range:\\n            for beta in beta_range:\\n                probs, _ = tec_calibration(val_logits, T_0, alpha, beta)\\n                ece = compute_ece(probs, val_labels)\\n                \\n                if ece < best_ece:\\n                    best_ece = ece\\n                    best_params = (T_0, alpha, beta)\\n    \\n    return best_params, best_ece\\n```\\n\\n### Heterogeneous Split Creation\\n```python\\ndef create_heterogeneous_splits(logits, labels, easy_ratio=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Split dataset into easy (high margin) and hard (low margin) examples.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits\\n        labels: True labels\\n        easy_ratio: Ratio of easy examples to include\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        easy_indices, hard_indices\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Sort by margin\\n    sorted_indices = torch.argsort(margin, descending=True)\\n    \\n    n_easy = int(len(sorted_indices) * easy_ratio)\\n    easy_indices = sorted_indices[:n_easy]\\n    hard_indices = sorted_indices[n_easy:]\\n    \\n    return easy_indices, hard_indices\\n```\\n\\n### Metrics Computation\\n```python\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import brier_score_loss\\n\\ndef compute_ece(probs, labels, n_bins=10):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Expected Calibration Error.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_bins: Number of bins for calibration\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        ECE value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Get confidence and predictions\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values.numpy()\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1).numpy()\\n    labels = np.array(labels)\\n    \\n    # Bin predictions\\n    bins = np.linspace(0, 1, n_bins + 1)\\n    ece = 0.0\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bins):\\n        mask = (confs >= bins[i]) & (confs < bins[i + 1])\\n        if mask.sum() > 0:\\n            bin_acc = np.mean(preds[mask] == labels[mask])\\n            bin_conf = np.mean(confs[mask])\\n            ece += np.abs(bin_acc - bin_conf) * mask.sum() / len(confs)\\n    \\n    return ece\\n\\ndef compute_nll(probs, labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Negative Log-Likelihood.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, min=1e-12, max=1.0)\\n    labels = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    nll = -torch.log(probs[torch.arange(len(labels)), labels]).mean()\\n    return nll.item()\\n\\ndef compute_brier_score(probs, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Brier Score.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # One-hot encode labels\\n    labels_onehot = torch.zeros(len(labels), n_classes)\\n    labels_onehot.scatter_(1, torch.tensor(labels).unsqueeze(1), 1)\\n    \\n    brier = torch.mean((probs - labels_onehot) ** 2).item()\\n    return brier\\n\\ndef bootstrap_ci(metric_func, probs, labels, n_bootstrap=1000, confidence=0.95):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute bootstrap confidence interval for a metric.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        metric_func: Function that computes metric\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities\\n        labels: True labels\\n        n_bootstrap: Number of bootstrap samples\\n        confidence: Confidence level\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (mean, lower_ci, upper_ci)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs_np = probs.numpy()\\n    labels_np = np.array(labels)\\n    n = len(labels_np)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = []\\n    for _ in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        boot_probs = probs_np[indices]\\n        boot_labels = labels_np[indices]\\n        metric = metric_func(torch.tensor(boot_probs), boot_labels)\\n        bootstrap_metrics.append(metric)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = np.array(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    mean = np.mean(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    lower = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 - confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    upper = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 + confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    \\n    return mean, lower, upper\\n```\\n\\n### Main Experiment Loop\\n```python\\ndef run_experiment(dataset_name, logits, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Run full experiment for one dataset.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        dataset_name: Name of dataset\\n        logits: Extracted logits (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_classes: Number of classes\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Dictionary of results\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Split data\\n    n = len(labels)\\n    indices = np.random.permutation(n)\\n    train_idx = indices[:int(0.6 * n)]\\n    val_idx = indices[int(0.6 * n):int(0.8 * n)]\\n    test_idx = indices[int(0.8 * n):]\\n    \\n    # Prepare splits\\n    train_logits = [logits[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    train_labels = [labels[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    val_logits = [logits[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    val_labels = [labels[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    test_logits = [logits[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    test_labels = [labels[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    \\n    results = {'dataset': dataset_name}\\n    \\n    # Method 1: Uncalibrated\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Uncalibrated ===\\\")\\n    test_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(test_logits), dim=-1)\\n    test_preds = torch.argmax(test_probs, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece = compute_ece(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    brier = compute_brier_score(test_probs, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll = compute_nll(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    acc = (test_preds == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['uncalibrated'] = {\\n        'ece': ece,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci,\\n        'brier': brier,\\n        'nll': nll,\\n        'accuracy': acc\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 2: Temperature Scaling\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Temperature Scaling ===\\\")\\n    T_opt, val_preds, val_confs, val_probs = temperature_scaling(\\n        val_logits, val_labels, val_logits, val_labels\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal T to test set\\n    test_scaled = torch.tensor(test_logits) / T_opt\\n    test_probs_ts = torch.softmax(test_scaled, dim=-1)\\n    test_preds_ts = torch.argmax(test_probs_ts, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_ts = compute_ece(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    brier_ts = compute_brier_score(test_probs_ts, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_ts = compute_nll(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    acc_ts = (test_preds_ts == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_ts = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['temperature_scaling'] = {\\n        'T_optimal': T_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_ts,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_ts,\\n        'brier': brier_ts,\\n        'nll': nll_ts,\\n        'accuracy': acc_ts\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 3: TEC\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: TEC ===\\\")\\n    best_params, best_ece_val = tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels)\\n    T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt = best_params\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal TEC to test set\\n    test_probs_tec, test_T_sample = tec_calibration(\\n        test_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n    )\\n    test_preds_tec = torch.argmax(test_probs_tec, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_tec = compute_ece(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    brier_tec = compute_brier_score(test_probs_tec, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_tec = compute_nll(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    acc_tec = (test_preds_tec == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_tec = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['tec'] = {\\n        'T_0_optimal': T_0_opt,\\n        'alpha_optimal': alpha_opt,\\n        'beta_optimal': beta_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_tec,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_tec,\\n        'brier': brier_tec,\\n        'nll': nll_tec,\\n        'accuracy': acc_tec\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Heterogeneous Split Analysis\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Heterogeneous Split Analysis ===\\\")\\n    easy_idx, hard_idx = create_heterogeneous_splits(test_logits, test_labels)\\n    \\n    for split_name, split_idx in [('easy', easy_idx), ('hard', hard_idx)]:\\n        split_logits = [test_logits[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        split_labels = [test_labels[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        \\n        # Uncalibrated\\n        split_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(split_logits), dim=-1)\\n        ece_split = compute_ece(split_probs, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TS\\n        split_scaled = torch.tensor(split_logits) / T_opt\\n        split_probs_ts = torch.softmax(split_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        ece_ts_split = compute_ece(split_probs_ts, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TEC\\n        split_probs_tec, _ = tec_calibration(\\n            split_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n        )\\n        ece_tec_split = compute_ece(split_probs_tec, split_labels)\\n        \\n        results[f'heterogeneous_{split_name}'] = {\\n            'n_samples': len(split_idx),\\n            'uncalibrated_ece': ece_split,\\n            'ts_ece': ece_ts_split,\\n            'tec_ece': ece_tec_split\\n        }\\n    \\n    return results\\n```\\n\\n### Output Format\\n```python\\ndef save_results(all_results, filename='method_out.json'):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Save results to method_out.json.\\n    \\n    Format:\\n    {\\n        \\\"experiment\\\": \\\"TEC_vs_TS_evaluation\\\",\\n        \\\"datasets\\\": [\\n            {\\n                \\\"dataset\\\": \\\"sst-2\\\",\\n                \\\"n_classes\\\": 2,\\n                \\\"results\\\": {\\n                    \\\"uncalibrated\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"temperature_scaling\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"tec\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_easy\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_hard\\\": {...}\\n                }\\n            },\\n            ...\\n        ],\\n        \\\"summary\\\": {\\n            \\\"teec_better_than_ts_count\\\": 2,\\n            \\\"ts_better_than_teec_count\\\": 3,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_ts\\\": 0.05,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_tec\\\": 0.03\\n        }\\n    }\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    with open(filename, 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(all_results, f, indent=2)\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## Fallback Plan\\n\\n### Issue 1: Pre-trained Models Not Available/Fail to Load\\n**Symptoms:** Unable to load HuggingFace models, model download fails, out of memory.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. {"content": [{"cache_prompt": false, "type": "text", "text": "Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_3fUR0i5e8NC7/3_invention_loop/iter_2/gen_plan/gen_plan_experiment_1/.sdk_openhands_agent_struct_out.json:\n     1\t{\n     2\t  \"title\": \"Evaluate TEC vs TS Calibration on LLM Embeddings\",\n     3\t  \"summary\": \"Test thermodynamic entropy calibration against temperature scaling on 5 text classification datasets using pre-trained transformers, with heterogeneous split analysis and bootstrap confidence intervals.\",\n     4\t  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"gpu\",\n     5\t  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Experimental Setup\\n\\n### Dataset Preparation\\n1. Load the standardized datasets from the dependency artifact (full_data_out.json)\\n2. For each dataset, load the appropriate pre-trained model:\\n   - SST-2: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english\\n   - QNLI: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english (or BERT-base)\\n   - AG News: roberta-base (fine-tuned on AG News)\\n   - MNLI: roberta-large-mnli (or roberta-base)\\n   - DBpedia: bert-base-uncased (fine-tuned on DBpedia)\\n3. Split each dataset into:\\n   - Train (60%): for model fine-tuning if needed\\n   - Validation (20%): for hyperparameter tuning\\n   - Test (20%): for final evaluation\\n\\n### Model & Logit Extraction\\n```python\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import AutoModelForSequenceClassification, AutoTokenizer\\nfrom torch.utils.data import DataLoader\\nimport json\\n\\n# Load dataset\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Model mapping\\ndataset_models = {\\n    'sst-2': 'distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english',\\n    'qnli': 'bert-base-uncased',  # May need QNLI fine-tuned version\\n    'ag_news': 'roberta-base',  # May need AG News fine-tuned\\n    'mnli': 'roberta-large-mnli',\\n    'dbpedia': 'bert-base-uncased'  # May need DBpedia fine-tuned\\n}\\n\\n# Extract logits for each dataset\\nfor dataset_name, model_name in dataset_models.items():\\n    tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model = AutoModelForSequenceClassification.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model.eval()\\n    \\n    # Get dataset examples\\n    dataset = [d for d in data['datasets'] if d['dataset'] == dataset_name][0]\\n    examples = dataset['examples']\\n    \\n    # Extract logits (no gradient)\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        for ex in examples:\\n            inputs = tokenizer(ex['input'], return_tensors='pt', truncation=True, padding=True)\\n            outputs = model(**inputs)\\n            logits = outputs.logits\\n            # Store logits with example\\n            ex['logits'] = logits.numpy().tolist()\\n            ex['num_classes'] = logits.shape[-1]\\n```\\n\\n### Method 1: Uncalibrated Baseline\\n```python\\ndef uncalibrated_predictions(logits):\\n    # Softmax without temperature scaling\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1)\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values\\n    return preds, confs, probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 2: Temperature Scaling (TS)\\n```python\\nimport torch.nn as nn\\nimport torch.optim as optim\\n\\ndef temperature_scaling(logits, labels, val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Tune temperature T on validation set to minimize NLL.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Initialize temperature\\n    temperature = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1) * 1.0)\\n    optimizer = optim.LBFGS([temperature], lr=0.01, max_iter=50)\\n    \\n    logits_tensor = torch.tensor(logits)\\n    labels_tensor = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    \\n    def eval():\\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\\n        scaled_logits = logits_tensor / temperature\\n        loss = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()(scaled_logits, labels_tensor)\\n        loss.backward()\\n        return loss\\n    \\n    # Optimize temperature\\n    for _ in range(100):\\n        optimizer.step(eval)\\n    \\n    # Apply to validation set\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        val_scaled = torch.tensor(val_logits) / temperature\\n        val_probs = torch.softmax(val_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        val_preds = torch.argmax(val_probs, dim=-1)\\n        val_confs = torch.max(val_probs, dim=-1).values\\n    \\n    return temperature.item(), val_preds, val_confs, val_probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 3: Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration (TEC)\\n```python\\ndef compute_entropy(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Shannon entropy of probability distribution.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    epsilon = 1e-12\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, epsilon, 1.0 - epsilon)\\n    entropy = -torch.sum(probs * torch.log(probs), dim=-1)\\n    return entropy\\n\\ndef compute_margin(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute decision margin (difference between top-2 predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sorted_probs, _ = torch.sort(probs, dim=-1, descending=True)\\n    margin = sorted_probs[..., 0] - sorted_probs[..., 1]\\n    return margin\\n\\ndef tec_calibration(logits, T_0, alpha, beta):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration.\\n    \\n    Adjusts per-sample temperature based on entropy and margin:\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy - beta * margin)\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits (N, C)\\n        T_0: Base temperature parameter\\n        alpha: Entropy weight parameter\\n        beta: Margin weight parameter\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Calibrated probabilities\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    entropy = compute_entropy(probs)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Normalize entropy and margin to [0, 1]\\n    max_entropy = torch.log(torch.tensor(probs.shape[-1]).float())\\n    norm_entropy = entropy / max_entropy\\n    norm_margin = margin  # Already in [0, 1]\\n    \\n    # Compute per-sample temperature\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * norm_entropy - beta * norm_margin)\\n    T_sample = torch.clamp(T_sample, min=0.01, max=100.0)  # Prevent extremes\\n    \\n    # Apply temperature scaling per sample\\n    # Initialize temperature\\n    temperature = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1) * 1.0)\\n    optimizer = optim.LBFGS([temperature], lr=0.01, max_iter=50)\\n    \\n    logits_tensor = torch.tensor(logits)\\n    labels_tensor = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    \\n    def eval():\\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\\n        scaled_logits = logits_tensor / temperature\\n        loss = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()(scaled_logits, labels_tensor)\\n        loss.backward()\\n        return loss\\n    \\n    # Optimize temperature\\n    for _ in range(100):\\n        optimizer.step(eval)\\n    \\n    # Apply to validation set\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        val_scaled = torch.tensor(val_logits) / temperature\\n        val_probs = torch.softmax(val_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        val_preds = torch.argmax(val_probs, dim=-1)\\n        val_confs = torch.max(val_probs, dim=-1).values\\n    \\n    return temperature.item(), val_preds, val_confs, val_probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 3: Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration (TEC)\\n```python\\ndef compute_entropy(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Shannon entropy of probability distribution.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    epsilon = 1e-12\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, epsilon, 1.0 - epsilon)\\n    entropy = -torch.sum(probs * torch.log(probs), dim=-1)\\n    return entropy\\n\\ndef compute_margin(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute decision margin (difference between top-2 predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sorted_probs, _ = torch.sort(probs, dim=-1, descending=True)\\n    margin = sorted_probs[..., 0] - sorted_probs[..., 1]\\n    return margin\\n\\ndef tec_calibration(logits, T_0, alpha, beta):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration.\\n    \\n    Adjusts per-sample temperature based on entropy and margin:\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy - beta * margin)\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits (N, C)\\n        T_0: Base temperature parameter\\n        alpha: Entropy weight parameter\\n        beta: Margin weight parameter\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Calibrated probabilities\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    entropy = compute_entropy(probs)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Normalize entropy and margin to [0, 1]\\n    max_entropy = torch.log(torch.tensor(probs.shape[-1]).float())\\n    norm_entropy = entropy / max_entropy\\n    norm_margin = margin  # Already in [0, 1]\\n    \\n    # Compute per-sample temperature\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * norm_entropy - beta * norm_margin)\\n    T_sample = torch.clamp(T_sample, min=0.01, max=100.0)  # Prevent extremes\\n    \\n    # Apply temperature scaling per sample\\n    # Need to handle per-sample temperature\\n    scaled_logits = torch.tensor(logits) / T_sample.unsqueeze(-1)\\n    calibrated_probs = torch.softmax(scaled_logits, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    return calibrated_probs, T_sample\\n\\ndef tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Grid search for TEC hyperparameters.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    best_ece = float('inf')\\n    best_params = None\\n    \\n    T_0_range = [0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, 10.0, 20.0]\\n    alpha_range = [0.0, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0]\\n    beta_range = [0.0, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1.0]\\n    \\n    for T_0 in T_0_range:\\n        for alpha in alpha_range:\\n            for beta in beta_range:\\n                probs, _ = tec_calibration(val_logits, T_0, alpha, beta)\\n                ece = compute_ece(probs, val_labels)\\n                \\n                if ece < best_ece:\\n                    best_ece = ece\\n                    best_params = (T_0, alpha, beta)\\n    \\n    return best_params, best_ece\\n```\\n\\n### Heterogeneous Split Creation\\n```python\\ndef create_heterogeneous_splits(logits, labels, easy_ratio=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Split dataset into easy (high margin) and hard (low margin) examples.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits\\n        labels: True labels\\n        easy_ratio: Ratio of easy examples to include\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        easy_indices, hard_indices\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Sort by margin\\n    sorted_indices = torch.argsort(margin, descending=True)\\n    \\n    n_easy = int(len(sorted_indices) * easy_ratio)\\n    easy_indices = sorted_indices[:n_easy]\\n    hard_indices = sorted_indices[n_easy:]\\n    \\n    return easy_indices, hard_indices\\n```\\n\\n### Metrics Computation\\n```python\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import brier_score_loss\\n\\ndef compute_ece(probs, labels, n_bins=10):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Expected Calibration Error.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_bins: Number of bins for calibration\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        ECE value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # error occurs, switch to CPU fallback\\n- If time exceeds 5 hours, stop and save partial results\",\n     6\t\nReview the changes and make sure they are as expected. Edit the file again if necessary."}], "is_error": false, "command": "str_replace", "path": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_3fUR0i5e8NC7/3_invention_loop/iter_2/gen_plan/gen_plan_experiment_1/.sdk_openhands_agent_struct_out.json", "prev_exist": true, "old_content": "{\n  \"title\": \"Evaluate TEC vs TS Calibration on LLM Embeddings\",\n  \"summary\": \"Test thermodynamic entropy calibration against temperature scaling on 5 text classification datasets using pre-trained transformers, with heterogeneous split analysis and bootstrap confidence intervals.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"gpu\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Experimental Setup\\n\\n### Dataset Preparation\\n1. Load the standardized datasets from the dependency artifact (full_data_out.json)\\n2. For each dataset, load the appropriate pre-trained model:\\n   - SST-2: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english\\n   - QNLI: distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english (or BERT-base)\\n   - AG News: roberta-base (fine-tuned on AG News)\\n   - MNLI: roberta-large-mnli (or roberta-base)\\n   - DBpedia: bert-base-uncased (fine-tuned on DBpedia)\\n3. Split each dataset into:\\n   - Train (60%): for model fine-tuning if needed\\n   - Validation (20%): for hyperparameter tuning\\n   - Test (20%): for final evaluation\\n\\n### Model & Logit Extraction\\n```python\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import AutoModelForSequenceClassification, AutoTokenizer\\nfrom torch.utils.data import DataLoader\\nimport json\\n\\n# Load dataset\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Model mapping\\ndataset_models = {\\n    'sst-2': 'distilbert-base-uncased-finetuned-sst-2-english',\\n    'qnli': 'bert-base-uncased',  # May need QNLI fine-tuned version\\n    'ag_news': 'roberta-base',  # May need AG News fine-tuned\\n    'mnli': 'roberta-large-mnli',\\n    'dbpedia': 'bert-base-uncased'  # May need DBpedia fine-tuned\\n}\\n\\n# Extract logits for each dataset\\nfor dataset_name, model_name in dataset_models.items():\\n    tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model = AutoModelForSequenceClassification.from_pretrained(model_name)\\n    model.eval()\\n    \\n    # Get dataset examples\\n    dataset = [d for d in data['datasets'] if d['dataset'] == dataset_name][0]\\n    examples = dataset['examples']\\n    \\n    # Extract logits (no gradient)\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        for ex in examples:\\n            inputs = tokenizer(ex['input'], return_tensors='pt', truncation=True, padding=True)\\n            outputs = model(**inputs)\\n            logits = outputs.logits\\n            # Store logits with example\\n            ex['logits'] = logits.numpy().tolist()\\n            ex['num_classes'] = logits.shape[-1]\\n```\\n\\n### Method 1: Uncalibrated Baseline\\n```python\\ndef uncalibrated_predictions(logits):\\n    # Softmax without temperature scaling\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1)\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values\\n    return preds, confs, probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 2: Temperature Scaling (TS)\\n```python\\nimport torch.nn as nn\\nimport torch.optim as optim\\n\\ndef temperature_scaling(logits, labels, val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Tune temperature T on validation set to minimize NLL.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Initialize temperature\\n    temperature = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1) * 1.0)\\n    optimizer = optim.LBFGS([temperature], lr=0.01, max_iter=50)\\n    \\n    logits_tensor = torch.tensor(logits)\\n    labels_tensor = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    \\n    def eval():\\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\\n        scaled_logits = logits_tensor / temperature\\n        loss = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()(scaled_logits, labels_tensor)\\n        loss.backward()\\n        return loss\\n    \\n    # Optimize temperature\\n    for _ in range(100):\\n        optimizer.step(eval)\\n    \\n    # Apply to validation set\\n    with torch.no_grad():\\n        val_scaled = torch.tensor(val_logits) / temperature\\n        val_probs = torch.softmax(val_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        val_preds = torch.argmax(val_probs, dim=-1)\\n        val_confs = torch.max(val_probs, dim=-1).values\\n    \\n    return temperature.item(), val_preds, val_confs, val_probs\\n```\\n\\n### Method 3: Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration (TEC)\\n```python\\ndef compute_entropy(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Shannon entropy of probability distribution.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    epsilon = 1e-12\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, epsilon, 1.0 - epsilon)\\n    entropy = -torch.sum(probs * torch.log(probs), dim=-1)\\n    return entropy\\n\\ndef compute_margin(probs):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute decision margin (difference between top-2 predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sorted_probs, _ = torch.sort(probs, dim=-1, descending=True)\\n    margin = sorted_probs[..., 0] - sorted_probs[..., 1]\\n    return margin\\n\\ndef tec_calibration(logits, T_0, alpha, beta):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Thermodynamic Entropy Calibration.\\n    \\n    Adjusts per-sample temperature based on entropy and margin:\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * entropy - beta * margin)\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits (N, C)\\n        T_0: Base temperature parameter\\n        alpha: Entropy weight parameter\\n        beta: Margin weight parameter\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Calibrated probabilities\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    entropy = compute_entropy(probs)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Normalize entropy and margin to [0, 1]\\n    max_entropy = torch.log(torch.tensor(probs.shape[-1]).float())\\n    norm_entropy = entropy / max_entropy\\n    norm_margin = margin  # Already in [0, 1]\\n    \\n    # Compute per-sample temperature\\n    T_sample = T_0 * (1 + alpha * norm_entropy - beta * norm_margin)\\n    T_sample = torch.clamp(T_sample, min=0.01, max=100.0)  # Prevent extremes\\n    \\n    # Apply temperature scaling per sample\\n    # Need to handle per-sample temperature\\n    scaled_logits = torch.tensor(logits) / T_sample.unsqueeze(-1)\\n    calibrated_probs = torch.softmax(scaled_logits, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    return calibrated_probs, T_sample\\n\\ndef tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Grid search for TEC hyperparameters.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    best_ece = float('inf')\\n    best_params = None\\n    \\n    T_0_range = [0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, 10.0, 20.0]\\n    alpha_range = [0.0, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0]\\n    beta_range = [0.0, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1.0]\\n    \\n    for T_0 in T_0_range:\\n        for alpha in alpha_range:\\n            for beta in beta_range:\\n                probs, _ = tec_calibration(val_logits, T_0, alpha, beta)\\n                ece = compute_ece(probs, val_labels)\\n                \\n                if ece < best_ece:\\n                    best_ece = ece\\n                    best_params = (T_0, alpha, beta)\\n    \\n    return best_params, best_ece\\n```\\n\\n### Heterogeneous Split Creation\\n```python\\ndef create_heterogeneous_splits(logits, labels, easy_ratio=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Split dataset into easy (high margin) and hard (low margin) examples.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        logits: Raw logits\\n        labels: True labels\\n        easy_ratio: Ratio of easy examples to include\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        easy_indices, hard_indices\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(logits), dim=-1)\\n    margin = compute_margin(probs)\\n    \\n    # Sort by margin\\n    sorted_indices = torch.argsort(margin, descending=True)\\n    \\n    n_easy = int(len(sorted_indices) * easy_ratio)\\n    easy_indices = sorted_indices[:n_easy]\\n    hard_indices = sorted_indices[n_easy:]\\n    \\n    return easy_indices, hard_indices\\n```\\n\\n### Metrics Computation\\n```python\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import brier_score_loss\\n\\ndef compute_ece(probs, labels, n_bins=10):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Expected Calibration Error.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_bins: Number of bins for calibration\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        ECE value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Get confidence and predictions\\n    confs = torch.max(probs, dim=-1).values.numpy()\\n    preds = torch.argmax(probs, dim=-1).numpy()\\n    labels = np.array(labels)\\n    \\n    # Bin predictions\\n    bins = np.linspace(0, 1, n_bins + 1)\\n    ece = 0.0\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bins):\\n        mask = (confs >= bins[i]) & (confs < bins[i + 1])\\n        if mask.sum() > 0:\\n            bin_acc = np.mean(preds[mask] == labels[mask])\\n            bin_conf = np.mean(confs[mask])\\n            ece += np.abs(bin_acc - bin_conf) * mask.sum() / len(confs)\\n    \\n    return ece\\n\\ndef compute_nll(probs, labels):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Negative Log-Likelihood.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs = torch.clamp(probs, min=1e-12, max=1.0)\\n    labels = torch.tensor(labels)\\n    nll = -torch.log(probs[torch.arange(len(labels)), labels]).mean()\\n    return nll.item()\\n\\ndef compute_brier_score(probs, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Brier Score.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # One-hot encode labels\\n    labels_onehot = torch.zeros(len(labels), n_classes)\\n    labels_onehot.scatter_(1, torch.tensor(labels).unsqueeze(1), 1)\\n    \\n    brier = torch.mean((probs - labels_onehot) ** 2).item()\\n    return brier\\n\\ndef bootstrap_ci(metric_func, probs, labels, n_bootstrap=1000, confidence=0.95):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute bootstrap confidence interval for a metric.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        metric_func: Function that computes metric\\n        probs: Predicted probabilities\\n        labels: True labels\\n        n_bootstrap: Number of bootstrap samples\\n        confidence: Confidence level\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (mean, lower_ci, upper_ci)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    probs_np = probs.numpy()\\n    labels_np = np.array(labels)\\n    n = len(labels_np)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = []\\n    for _ in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        boot_probs = probs_np[indices]\\n        boot_labels = labels_np[indices]\\n        metric = metric_func(torch.tensor(boot_probs), boot_labels)\\n        bootstrap_metrics.append(metric)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_metrics = np.array(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    mean = np.mean(bootstrap_metrics)\\n    lower = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 - confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    upper = np.percentile(bootstrap_metrics, (1 + confidence) / 2 * 100)\\n    \\n    return mean, lower, upper\\n```\\n\\n### Main Experiment Loop\\n```python\\ndef run_experiment(dataset_name, logits, labels, n_classes):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Run full experiment for one dataset.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        dataset_name: Name of dataset\\n        logits: Extracted logits (N, C)\\n        labels: True labels (N,)\\n        n_classes: Number of classes\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        Dictionary of results\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Split data\\n    n = len(labels)\\n    indices = np.random.permutation(n)\\n    train_idx = indices[:int(0.6 * n)]\\n    val_idx = indices[int(0.6 * n):int(0.8 * n)]\\n    test_idx = indices[int(0.8 * n):]\\n    \\n    # Prepare splits\\n    train_logits = [logits[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    train_labels = [labels[i] for i in train_idx]\\n    val_logits = [logits[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    val_labels = [labels[i] for i in val_idx]\\n    test_logits = [logits[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    test_labels = [labels[i] for i in test_idx]\\n    \\n    results = {'dataset': dataset_name}\\n    \\n    # Method 1: Uncalibrated\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Uncalibrated ===\\\")\\n    test_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(test_logits), dim=-1)\\n    test_preds = torch.argmax(test_probs, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece = compute_ece(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    brier = compute_brier_score(test_probs, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll = compute_nll(test_probs, test_labels)\\n    acc = (test_preds == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['uncalibrated'] = {\\n        'ece': ece,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci,\\n        'brier': brier,\\n        'nll': nll,\\n        'accuracy': acc\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 2: Temperature Scaling\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Temperature Scaling ===\\\")\\n    T_opt, val_preds, val_confs, val_probs = temperature_scaling(\\n        val_logits, val_labels, val_logits, val_labels\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal T to test set\\n    test_scaled = torch.tensor(test_logits) / T_opt\\n    test_probs_ts = torch.softmax(test_scaled, dim=-1)\\n    test_preds_ts = torch.argmax(test_probs_ts, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_ts = compute_ece(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    brier_ts = compute_brier_score(test_probs_ts, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_ts = compute_nll(test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    acc_ts = (test_preds_ts == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_ts = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_ts, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['temperature_scaling'] = {\\n        'T_optimal': T_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_ts,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_ts,\\n        'brier': brier_ts,\\n        'nll': nll_ts,\\n        'accuracy': acc_ts\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Method 3: TEC\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: TEC ===\\\")\\n    best_params, best_ece_val = tune_tec_hyperparameters(val_logits, val_labels)\\n    T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt = best_params\\n    \\n    # Apply optimal TEC to test set\\n    test_probs_tec, test_T_sample = tec_calibration(\\n        test_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n    )\\n    test_preds_tec = torch.argmax(test_probs_tec, dim=-1)\\n    \\n    ece_tec = compute_ece(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    brier_tec = compute_brier_score(test_probs_tec, test_labels, n_classes)\\n    nll_tec = compute_nll(test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    acc_tec = (test_preds_tec == torch.tensor(test_labels)).float().mean().item()\\n    \\n    ece_ci_tec = bootstrap_ci(compute_ece, test_probs_tec, test_labels)\\n    \\n    results['tec'] = {\\n        'T_0_optimal': T_0_opt,\\n        'alpha_optimal': alpha_opt,\\n        'beta_optimal': beta_opt,\\n        'ece': ece_tec,\\n        'ece_ci': ece_ci_tec,\\n        'brier': brier_tec,\\n        'nll': nll_tec,\\n        'accuracy': acc_tec\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Heterogeneous Split Analysis\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\n=== {dataset_name}: Heterogeneous Split Analysis ===\\\")\\n    easy_idx, hard_idx = create_heterogeneous_splits(test_logits, test_labels)\\n    \\n    for split_name, split_idx in [('easy', easy_idx), ('hard', hard_idx)]:\\n        split_logits = [test_logits[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        split_labels = [test_labels[i] for i in split_idx]\\n        \\n        # Uncalibrated\\n        split_probs = torch.softmax(torch.tensor(split_logits), dim=-1)\\n        ece_split = compute_ece(split_probs, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TS\\n        split_scaled = torch.tensor(split_logits) / T_opt\\n        split_probs_ts = torch.softmax(split_scaled, dim=-1)\\n        ece_ts_split = compute_ece(split_probs_ts, split_labels)\\n        \\n        # TEC\\n        split_probs_tec, _ = tec_calibration(\\n            split_logits, T_0_opt, alpha_opt, beta_opt\\n        )\\n        ece_tec_split = compute_ece(split_probs_tec, split_labels)\\n        \\n        results[f'heterogeneous_{split_name}'] = {\\n            'n_samples': len(split_idx),\\n            'uncalibrated_ece': ece_split,\\n            'ts_ece': ece_ts_split,\\n            'tec_ece': ece_tec_split\\n        }\\n    \\n    return results\\n```\\n\\n### Output Format\\n```python\\ndef save_results(all_results, filename='method_out.json'):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Save results to method_out.json.\\n    \\n    Format:\\n    {\\n        \\\"experiment\\\": \\\"TEC_vs_TS_evaluation\\\",\\n        \\\"datasets\\\": [\\n            {\\n                \\\"dataset\\\": \\\"sst-2\\\",\\n                \\\"n_classes\\\": 2,\\n                \\\"results\\\": {\\n                    \\\"uncalibrated\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"temperature_scaling\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"tec\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_easy\\\": {...},\\n                    \\\"heterogeneous_hard\\\": {...}\\n                }\\n            },\\n            ...\\n        ],\\n        \\\"summary\\\": {\\n            \\\"teec_better_than_ts_count\\\": 2,\\n            \\\"ts_better_than_teec_count\\\": 3,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_ts\\\": 0.05,\\n            \\\"average_ece_improvement_tec\\\": 0.03\\n        }\\n    }\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    with open(filename, 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(all_results, f, indent=2)\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## Fallback Plan\\n\\n### Issue 1: Pre-trained Models Not Available/Fail to Load\\n**Symptoms:** Unable to load HuggingFace models, model download fails, out of memory.\\n\\n**Fallback:**\\n1. passed!\\\")\\n```\\n\\n### Phase 7: Full Experiment Launch (remaining time)\\nIf all tests pass, launch full experiment on all 5 datasets.\\n\\n**Monitoring:**\\n- Check GPU memory usage (should be <
